  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a944c613-5ee2-4768-a461-e9969378c614'
      });
    }

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1402370-why-did-the-author-devote-half-to-book-to">Why did the author devote half to book to Hanna&#39;s point of view? Rarely did she sound like a seven year old but more like a nasty adult with an adult vocabulary. Also, Hanna&#39;s inability to speak was never explained. Nevertheless despite these major flaws I thoroughly enjoyed the book.</a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/28100473-keerie-prasopoulos"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1453220259i/28100473._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/28100473-keerie-prasopoulos">Keerie Prasopoulos</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hannah’s point of view was important to the story to prove that this character had some deep psychological issues. Often books are written with a devi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hannah’s point of view was important to the story to prove that this character had some deep psychological issues. Often books are written with a devious child and it is the mother that is the one who is imaging the deception. One of the professional characters in this book explains Hannah’s nonverbal behaviors. She is manipulative and aware of all she does, not a sweet innocent child.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2280938242?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="j e w e l s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="j e w e l s" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s">j e w e l s</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2280938242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2518850737212029487"><b> ONE STAR ⭐️ for me because I finished it!</b> <br/><br/>This book is trying so hard to be controversial. Instead, it's an epic fail. I'm not in the HATE it or LOVE it camp. <i>I'm in the incredibly bored and what is the point camp?.</i><br/><br/>In case you've been busy reading a good book (lucky you!) and missed some of the pre-hype, BABY TEETH is the story of a creepy seven-year old mute girl, Hanna, who hates her mommy and wants to kill her. She wants mommy out of the picture so that she can have daddy all to herself. Tha</span>
  <span id="freeText2518850737212029487" style="display:none"><b> ONE STAR ⭐️ for me because I finished it!</b> <br /><br />This book is trying so hard to be controversial. Instead, it's an epic fail. I'm not in the HATE it or LOVE it camp. <i>I'm in the incredibly bored and what is the point camp?.</i><br /><br />In case you've been busy reading a good book (lucky you!) and missed some of the pre-hype, BABY TEETH is the story of a creepy seven-year old mute girl, Hanna, who hates her mommy and wants to kill her. She wants mommy out of the picture so that she can have daddy all to herself. That's it. Seriously, that's the whole book! Hanna: silently plotting and planning her next mean thing to do to mommy. Mommy: wringing her hands and worrying why her daughter is so evil. Daddy: humming and happy, oblivious to the actual pain his adorable Hanna causes on others around her. <br /><br />Brace yourself, folks! St. Martin's Press is amping up for a full-on publicity assault to promote their summer baby. BABY TEETH (UK title: BAD APPLE) is set to be released in July 2018. <b>We are only human and you may become curious about all the hype on social media, DON'T BUY INTO IT!!!</b> <br /><br />Believe me. Don't waste your money or time on this dud. <b>Stay strong.</b> The book is deficient in every way. I heard it was shocking and disturbing...NO, it's not! I live for shocking and disturbing, this is not it! It's just dumb.<br /><br />There is something missing with this book, there is nothing there to hold your interest. I feel like Hanna should have been written with more of a horror bent, at least it would have spiced up the plot a bit. I spent the first half of the book wishing I could chalk it up as mindless entertainment, but it's missing the entertainment part. I found myself skimming out of boredom. No plot twist. No thriller. I didn’t feel tension or suspense. Dull as dishwater. <br /><br />I hate to finish like a negative Nancy. So, I add this: the cover is striking and I love the title! Too bad about the book.😕<br /><br /><i>Many thanks to NetGalley for allowing me to read this book and post my honest review!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2518850737212029487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer949664899610648079">READ THIS REVIEW AT YOUR OWN RISK.... SPOILERS +SPOILERS +SPOILERS...<br/>HOWEVER... I QUIT! I’m throwing in the towel. I’ve read enough...stopping at 41% on my Kindle copy. <br/>I appreciate the widget-offering from the publisher — but for me— I CAN’T compare this book to “The Dinner” ....or “We Need To Talk About Kevin”....Both of those two other books had a different quality and purpose IMO....<br/>THIS BOOK seems to me - to be an intentionally disturbing novel - for the pure pleasure of the thrill. It’s ug</span>
  <span id="freeText949664899610648079" style="display:none">READ THIS REVIEW AT YOUR OWN RISK.... SPOILERS +SPOILERS +SPOILERS...<br />HOWEVER... I QUIT! I’m throwing in the towel. I’ve read enough...stopping at 41% on my Kindle copy. <br />I appreciate the widget-offering from the publisher — but for me— I CAN’T compare this book to “The Dinner” ....or “We Need To Talk About Kevin”....Both of those two other books had a different quality and purpose IMO....<br />THIS BOOK seems to me - to be an intentionally disturbing novel - for the pure pleasure of the thrill. It’s ugly and non-inspiring. It ‘is’........absorbing.....but I’m not proud of myself reading it. <br />I choose to stop this nonsense- I don’t want to be a stand for books where children are evil — for the sake of psychological pleasure reading. <br />Even without finishing this book - I can already see the author isn’t accomplishing any attempts to portray what might lead a child to kill —- such as Lionel Shriver did in “We Need To Talk About Kevin”. It’s bumblegum chewing for the sake of chewing mindlessly. I’m not a fan— but many readers probably will be:<br /><br />HERE’S MY REVIEW.... all little Excepts..... NOTE: I DO NOT KNOW HOW THIS BOOK ENDS - perhaps a girlfriend will tell me later - save me the reading time - so that I can move on to a book that is a better fit for me.....<br /><br />Lots of SAMPLES to get a TASTE of what you’re in for if you choose to read this novel:<br />Mom says: <br /> “She never liked me. No, that’s not true. When she was a baby…Suzette knew she was oversharing, but the words spelled out. But at some point the war began. And I’m losing. I’m losing it. And I can’t tell my husband, I try but…He doesn’t see it. And where would I be? I’m supposed to be a good mom, the mom I never had, that’s what I wanted. That’s what I promised him, what I promised myself”. <br /><br />Mom says: <br /> “ I thought everything would get better. Kindergarten. But she didn’t talk. That’s how it all started. We tried doctors, there’s nothing physically wrong. But every place I’ve tried to enroll her, and every babysitter, it’s like she wants to torture— just me”. <br /><br />Dad says: <br /> “How’s my squirrely girl?” ...... Providing optimistic perky happiness of possibilities? —- sure ..... deny deny deny.... no problems with his little angle —- HANNA LOVES DADDY! I’m guessing ‘Daddy’ will face up to the problems pretty soon....but for now - he prefers to deny them. <br /><br />Hanna says: .....Thinking to herself <br /> “It remained disappointing that Daddy hadn’t let mommy wither and die when he had a chance”. ( note.. Hanna saw her parents having sex - she was hoping with dad on top of mom, he would kill her). Oh well! <br /> “As Hanna grew stronger she could take it advantage of Mommy’s weakness. Could mommy die if cleaning too much – – could she scrubbed to death? And <br />Mommy needed a lot of medication. If something bad happened to her medicine, would something bad happen to mommy?”<br /> “Or maybe...Mommy was always fussing about how she looked, and she glowed whenever Daddy said she was beautiful.”<br /> “Maybe If Mommy was uglier”<br /> “Maybe Daddy wouldn’t love her as much”. <br /><br />CHARMING HANNA...<br /> “She stuffed a grape in her mouth, a strawberry, a cheese cube, another cheese cube, another grape. And made a show at chewing, chewing.”<br /> “When it was a nice mushy consistency, Hanna got up on her knees and spit the whole glob in Mommy’s face. It struck her cheek, then started to dribble down. Hanna giggled”. <br /><br />CHARMING MOM.....<br /> “Mommy scooped the mash from her face. For a second Hanna thought she might cry. But Mommy got up and came around and forced the glob back into Hanna’s mouth.” She held her hand there, making it so Hanna couldn’t open her lips. <br />She couldn’t spit anything back out, but she could barely breathe. <br /> “CHEW”. <br /><br />Yuck!!! <br /> <br />1/2 STAR rating. <br /><br />Thank You Netgalley— St. Martin’s who I always appreciate- ( I’m so sorry - this book just wasn’t healthy for my soul), and Zoje Stage... there is not much I can’t hear - but I’m sorry - I just didn’t want to read any more. The scenes you picked to write for the child - the language from the mom - I just didn’t feel well reading your book. <br />But - good luck to you - I think many people actually gobble your novel up.</span>

<div id="review_2233928246" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2233928246" />
    <a title="Deanna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15662887-deanna"><img alt="Deanna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437589889p2/15662887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2233928246?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna " href="/user/show/15662887-deanna">Deanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15662887-deanna?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2233928246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9863100042578224511">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/'>https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br/><br/>OH MY ….<br/><br/>I have no words.<br/><br/>HA! Yeah right!!<br/><br/>Hanna LOVES her Daddy. Her Mommy?<br/><br/>Not so much….<br/><br/>This first thing I’m going to say about “Baby Teeth” is that it <strong>won’t be for everybody</strong>. And that’s OKAY! I’m not going to judge anyone for liking it OR not liking it. It’s a fiction book!<br/><br/>It does clearly say in the description:<br/><br/><strong>
  <em>“From blazing new talent Zoje Stage, Baby Teeth is a story about a perfect-looking family, and a darling little g</em></strong></span>
  <span id="freeText9863100042578224511" style="display:none">My reviews can also be seen at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpress.com/">https://deesradreadsandreviews.wordpr...</a><br /><br />OH MY ….<br /><br />I have no words.<br /><br />HA! Yeah right!!<br /><br />Hanna LOVES her Daddy. Her Mommy?<br /><br />Not so much….<br /><br />This first thing I’m going to say about “Baby Teeth” is that it <strong>won’t be for everybody</strong>. And that’s OKAY! I’m not going to judge anyone for liking it OR not liking it. It’s a fiction book!<br /><br />It does clearly say in the description:<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“From blazing new talent Zoje Stage, Baby Teeth is a story about a perfect-looking family, and a darling little girl who wants nothing more than to kill her mother.”</em>
</strong><br /><br />A book about a child wanting to kill their mother is not going to be light suspense…it’s likely going to be an uncomfortable read. So I knew what I was getting into…. for the most part.<br /><br />The book opens with Hanna at the hospital having a CT scan. It’s not her first. There have been many tests.<br /><br />You see….Hanna doesn’t speak.<br /><br /><strong>
  <em> “Words, ever unreliable, were no one’s friend”</em>
</strong><br /><br />Hanna knows how much Mommy wants her to talk.<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“Mommy was failing her tests to prove her motherly love.” </em>
</strong><br /><br />Is Hanna choosing not to talk?<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“if it’s a matter of her refusing…WON’T requires a different type of doctor than CAN’T.”</em>
</strong><br /><br />Hanna’s favorite game is “Scare Mommy” and she likes to make special projects for Mommy too. VERY special.<br /><br />WOW! I have such conflicting emotions about this one!<br /><br />Imagine having someone who you expect will love you, not love you. And not only do they not love you? They LOATHE you.<br /><br />They wish you didn’t exist….<br /><br />The story is told from Hanna and Suzette’s alternating perspectives. There are some terrifying and dysfunctional scenes in this book. I haven’t read “The Dinner” or “We Need to Talk About Kevin” (books that this has been compared to) so I wouldn’t know how it stacks up against them.<br /><br />“Baby Teeth” seems to be in its own league. A ball of darkness and wickedness that will make you squirm. I couldn’t put this sucker down. I read it in two sittings and honestly, when I wasn’t reading it, I was thinking about it.<br /><br />I wondered if a seven-year-old was capable of some of the acts committed. Could a child be that diabolical and manipulative? I think this is one of those books that if you look at it closely, yes you will probably see a lot of things that push the believability envelope…right off the table. However, it ended up not mattering if things were all possible or believable…. I was pulled right into the story.<br /><br />As I said earlier, this book won’t be for everyone. I do wonder if it would fit more into the horror genre. I found it diabolical and creepy and I’m really glad I read it. “Baby Teeth” is definitely a book I won’t soon forget. I’m very curious to see what Zoje Stage is going to come up with next.<br /><br />Thank you to St. Martin’s Press for the opportunity to read this book in exchange for my honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9863100042578224511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Crumb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53025065-crumb"><img alt="Crumb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514642499p2/53025065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2121800359?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crumb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crumb" href="/user/show/53025065-crumb">Crumb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2121800359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3225598298482853543"><b>A Sure-Fire Hit! Not to be Missed!</b><br/><br/>This is going to be one of the most controversial books of the year. It has generated a whole lot of buzz on social media and has garnered tons of reviews here on Goodreads. Whether you hate it or you love it, <i>you won't be able to stop talking about it</i>. So, you may as well read the book and see what the big deal is, right?<br/> <pre> * * * * * * * * * * * * </pre><br/><i>What would you do if your child hated you? Really and truly hated you? Hated you so much , in fact, that she wanted </i></span>
  <span id="freeText3225598298482853543" style="display:none"><b>A Sure-Fire Hit! Not to be Missed!</b><br><br>This is going to be one of the most controversial books of the year. It has generated a whole lot of buzz on social media and has garnered tons of reviews here on Goodreads. Whether you hate it or you love it, <i>you won't be able to stop talking about it</i>. So, you may as well read the book and see what the big deal is, right?<br> <pre> * * * * * * * * * * * * </pre><br><i>What would you do if your child hated you? Really and truly hated you? Hated you so much , in fact, that she wanted to eliminate you?</i><br><br>These are the questions that Suzette faces day in and day out. Her daughter is not her bouncy, red-cheeked little baby anymore. Her daughter, Hanna, is now a monster, a devil. <i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519391641ra/25109799.gif" width="350" height="240" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Here’s the catch: Hanna only behaves this way toward Suzette; nary a complaint toward her father, Alex.</i> The more alarming Hanna’s behavior becomes, the more sophisticated Hanna becomes at the art of manipulating her father, or as she likes to call him, her daddy. Her father is blind to Hanna’s cruelty and tricks. Hanna wants her daddy all to herself. <i>But, Suzette is in the way.</i><br>As the house starts to become increasingly volatile and claustrophobic, Suzette begins to wonder if she will ever feel safe in her own house, alone with her “baby daughter.”<br><br><b>Zoje Stage is fearless</b>. This book will surely be controversial and will likely be the subject of many heated debates among book clubs everywhere. I happened to love this book, but I recognize that this book isn’t for everyone. However, that’s why books are so special. <i>A thousand people can read one book and have several different opinions and perspectives</i>. I can’t imagine what Stage will turn out next, but, what I do know is, I will be the first in line!<br><br><b>Note: Carol and I read this together, as a buddy read. If you would like to view our discussion on this book, please <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/19226828-buddy-read-for-baby-teeth" rel="nofollow noopener"> Click Here </a> Anything that could be viewed as a spoiler is marked accordingly.</b><br><br><i>I received this as a courtesy from the publisher in exchange for an honest review </i></span>

<div id="review_2244764374" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2244764374" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2244764374?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=from-publisher-or-author">from-publisher-or-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=creepy-children">creepy-children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2244764374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4458844269881544670"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best horror 2018! what will happen?</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517228570i/24959289.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>this is the story of a seven-year-old girl named hanna who loves her daddy SO MUCH that she doesn’t want anyone else taking up any of his time or attention. so, obviously, her mom’s gotta go. like, go in a “not be breathing anymore” way.<br/><br/>in what is either a chilling declaration of intent or a genius marketing strategy, the author has dedicated this book to her father, which cracked me up.<br/><br/>because that’s the best way </span>
  <span id="freeText4458844269881544670" style="display:none"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best horror 2018! what will happen?</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1517228570i/24959289.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>this is the story of a seven-year-old girl named hanna who loves her daddy SO MUCH that she doesn’t want anyone else taking up any of his time or attention. so, obviously, her mom’s gotta go. like, go in a “not be breathing anymore” way.<br><br>in what is either a chilling declaration of intent or a genius marketing strategy, the author has dedicated this book to her father, which cracked me up.<br><br>because that’s the best way to appreciate this book, as the blackest comedy center wrapped up in a thin horror candyskin. it’s compared to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80660.We_Need_to_Talk_About_Kevin" title="We Need to Talk About Kevin by Lionel Shriver" rel="nofollow noopener">We Need to Talk About Kevin</a>, which i haven’t read, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15797938.The_Dinner" title="The Dinner by Herman Koch" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dinner</a>, which i have read and did not like, but i’m not sure these books are all playing to the same crowd. because while, yes, they all have “kids doing reprehensible things” at their center, it’s carried out in different angles of approach. there’s a world of difference between <i>The Bad Seed</i> and gus van sant’s <i>Elephant</i>, even though they hold hands over the “kids do the murderyest things” campfire. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/80660.We_Need_to_Talk_About_Kevin" title="We Need to Talk About Kevin by Lionel Shriver" rel="nofollow noopener">We Need to Talk About Kevin</a>, from what i understand, is an earnest attempt to understand what drives a child to orchestrate a school shooting, an exploration of parental guilt and culpability. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15797938.The_Dinner" title="The Dinner by Herman Koch" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dinner</a> is just nihilism on parade where everything is shitty in different ways and who even cares about anything? whereas this book has the following note-to-self:<br><br><i>Maybe it had been a mistake, trying to set Mommy on fire. If only she’d known how long it took for things - or people - to fully ignite.</i><br><br>it’s not a fun campy romp, but it’s also not an incisive psychological examination of sociopathy. it’s a back-and-forth POV between an exhausted, reluctant mother and a deeply manipulative little girl whose refusal to speak, although she does not lack the physical means, is at the center of their rift. each is frustrated by their inability to communicate, to be understood, trapped in the house with each other all day in a silent battle of wills, until daddy comes home with his smiles and his loving indulgence of hanna’s silence, seemingly inexhaustible because he only has to trot it our for an hour or two a day. fuck <i>that</i> guy, basically. <br><br>it’s a strong, if somewhat predictable, offering in the “creepy kids” genre. hanna is perfectly menacing, and her voice and reasoning skills are usually appropriate to her age, <i>Every win for Hanna was a you-lose for Mommy,</i> but there are a few moments that seem a little too much for a seven-year-old:<br><br> <i>Sometimes she wished she could remember being in Mommy’s tummy. Were they both really happy then? When their blood was all jumbled up and they shared a mystery?</i><br><br>the more childish the voice, the creepier it is. <br><br>suzette is a great dramatic counterpoint to hanna, and since the “creepy kid” is the constant in books like this, it is the parent’s reactions that determine where the book goes, so it’s all on her. which is a pretty constant theme in the book, along with parental breaking points.<br><br><i>It was hard to pour endless love into someone who wouldn’t love you back. No one could do it forever.</i><br><br>we do get insight into how this mother-daughter relationship has soured; the contributing misunderstandings, resentments, the unfulfilled hopes, plus suzette’s own poor excuse for a maternal role model and a life narrowed by illness in which she basically went from sickbed to marriage bed, so is more dependent on her husband than is seemly:<br><br><i>For a moment she was transported to the early days. The early nights. When he was everything. When she was someone. When the two of them were enough. And having a child meant the exponential increase of their love, because they wanted more ways to express it. Now they knew how a child divided them, as individuals, and a couple.</i><br><br>but really, this is all about a tiny monster, the people who love her, and why they totally should not.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517228570ra/24959290.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>fun creepy fun.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4458844269881544670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2286438311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2286438311" />
    <a title="Felice Laverne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50404233-felice-laverne"><img alt="Felice Laverne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548611171p2/50404233.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2286438311?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felice Laverne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felice Laverne" href="/user/show/50404233-felice-laverne">Felice Laverne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=waspy">waspy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=full-review">full-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=women-s-fiction">women-s-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=cozy-thriller">cozy-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50404233-felice-laverne?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2286438311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6365851804085586455"><i>Mommy was only a shell of a person with nothing to give. She was like a store full of bright and tempting candies held captive behind a thick, transparent wall. It wasn't like Hanna hadn't tried to tap on the glass and grasp what was inside.</i><br/><br/>So, it’s possible that I’m just too much of a Southerner for this book, but <i>Baby Teeth</i> absolutely did not work for me. (Well, that's not 100% true: I think the book's title and cover art are <b>phenomenal</b>.) It was just so melodramatic and implausible that I foun</span>
  <span id="freeText6365851804085586455" style="display:none"><i>Mommy was only a shell of a person with nothing to give. She was like a store full of bright and tempting candies held captive behind a thick, transparent wall. It wasn't like Hanna hadn't tried to tap on the glass and grasp what was inside.</i><br /><br />So, it’s possible that I’m just too much of a Southerner for this book, but <i>Baby Teeth</i> absolutely did not work for me. (Well, that's not 100% true: I think the book's title and cover art are <b>phenomenal</b>.) It was just so melodramatic and implausible that I found myself doing the deepest of eye rolls on more than one occasion, and turning the page became a harder and harder task the further I got along in this novel.<br /><br />The premise of this novel is very simple: A seven-year-old terrorizes her mother but puts on an innocent face for Daddy, driving a wedge between the couple and driving the mom to desperation. Think <i>The Orphan</i> (2009) meets <i>We Need to Talk About Kevin</i> (2011). With that out of the way, we can move on to the merits and non-redeeming qualities of this book, shall we?<br /><br />One of my pet peeves in fiction is when entire plot lines hinge on implausible circumstances. I heaved this book into that metaphorical pile pretty early on and it will remain there forever. <i>Baby Teeth</i> was kin to those horror movies where the pretty blonde girl is running through the night in her heels and instead of running outside of the house for safety, she runs upstairs to the collective annoyance of the audience. Like, the plot didn’t make ANY sense! Why, you may ask? Because the entire narrative would have been different if one of two SIMPLE things had happened: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ If Suzette had had the common sense to a) video record her daughter’s bad behavior to show her husband as proof or b) if she’d actually tried her hand at disciplining her. *side eye glance inserted here* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. That’s why I say I must be too much of a Southerner for this book, because I don’t know anyone, of any color or creed, who would let their kid get away with the things little Hanna got away with – and then <s>
  <i>crawl and <b>grovel</b> on their knees for this child’s forgiveness after THEY, the PARENT, have been assaulted</i>
</s>. Seriously, implausible. And, so weak-willed that I started to really despise Suzette's spinelessness. Spine. Less.<br /><br />Aside from the sheer improbability of this story line, it also wasn’t very well-written either. And, there are very few things more unforgivable than that to an avid reader. I mean, yes, there were words strung together in a way that made sense in the English language, but I didn’t feel that there was any remarkable skill on display whatsoever. I didn't feel like I'd stumbled across anything that I would take with me for more than 4 minutes after I turned the final page of that book. It read as a first-time novel for sure, clunky and clumsily done. <br /><br />I’ve seen <i>Baby Teeth</i> listed as a thriller; it wasn’t that at all, but it COULD have been. It probably would have been a much more enjoyable read—cringe-worthy moments in the plot and all—if it had been written from Suzette’s POV only. Then we could have seen her mounting terror and desperation and feel it in a more pure form—the way that she did. But Stage decided to try her hand at writing in a child’s voice via Hanna's chapters and it Did. Not. Work. Honestly, a terrible idea given the level of skill she displayed in this novel. Not only did it take away from the suspense to know exactly what Hanna was going to do next from her POV, but the clunky and inauthentic way in which Stage wrote Hanna made reading her chapters a real chore. Of course, I understand that Stage was attempting to speak simplistically, as a child might, but it didn’t sound anything like a seven-year-old’s way of speech and mannerisms in the slightest. Her editor would have done better to tell her to hold off on that.<br /><br />I nearly didn’t finish this book. I found it to be THAT ridiculous with nothing remarkable about the writing style to keep me hooked. But, as we readers often do, I just HAD to trudge on to see if my mind would be magically changed in the end. It wasn’t, though the end result of the book was one of the better parts of the plot, so at least there’s that, right? 2 stars **<br /><br />*I received an ARC of this book from the publisher, St. Martin's Press, via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br /><b>FOLLOW ME HERE:</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49185491-the-other-americans?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=tl37nwckP6&amp;rank=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/queenbee_fifi" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thefelicelaverne/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Other-Americans-Novel-Felice-Laverne/dp/1672094488/ref=sr_1_1?crid=25JA8C7GHLFY8&amp;keywords=the+other+americans+felice+laverne&amp;qid=1579649731&amp;sprefix=the+other+americans+felice%2Caps%2C208&amp;sr=8-1" rel="nofollow noopener">Get a Copy of My Book</a> | <a href="https://www.artanddecoagency.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Editing, Author Coaching, Submit Your Book to Me</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6365851804085586455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2286438311">

<div id="review_2268147997" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2268147997" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2268147997?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2268147997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7953669760089360961"><b>Bloody fantastic.</b> Perfect for fans of the Horror movies, <i>Orphan</i>, or <i>Case 39</i>.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550067575ra/27057343.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When Suzette becomes a first-time mother, she is excited and anxious, as any new mother would be. <br/><br/>She didn't have the greatest relationship with her own Mum and feels this is her chance to do better by her daughter.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550265349ra/27071662.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Suzette and her husband, Alex, work hard to provide their daughter, Hanna, a home she can grow and flourish in. <br/><br/>However, it becomes apparent fairly quickly that Hanna is not an ordinary child.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491401725ra/22407069.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Due to Hanna bein</span>
  <span id="freeText7953669760089360961" style="display:none"><b>Bloody fantastic.</b> Perfect for fans of the Horror movies, <i>Orphan</i>, or <i>Case 39</i>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550067575ra/27057343.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Suzette becomes a first-time mother, she is excited and anxious, as any new mother would be. <br><br>She didn't have the greatest relationship with her own Mum and feels this is her chance to do better by her daughter.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550265349ra/27071662.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Suzette and her husband, Alex, work hard to provide their daughter, Hanna, a home she can grow and flourish in. <br><br>However, it becomes apparent fairly quickly that Hanna is not an ordinary child.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491401725ra/22407069.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Due to Hanna being non-communicative and combative, Suzette is forced to keep her home and provide all of her schooling and care. <br><br>She doesn't want to do this. No one, including her husband, seems to understand what she has to go through every day.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1566503376ra/28035522.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She wants Hanna to go to school like the other children. She wants her to learn how to play and interact with others. <br><br>And, yes, let's be honest, get her out of her hair for a while, but Hanna has other plans.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480818983ra/21353548.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What transpired within these pages chilled me to the core. THE CORE. <br><br>This kid. Mmmmm, she is not messing around. I WANTED to get away from her and she's a fictional character.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1550265349ra/27071661.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This story is a story you think you know. It's the classic <i>The Omen</i> evil child trope, which frankly, is one of my favorites. <br><br>I don't think I am giving anything away by saying that. You can deem that much from reading the synopsis but this book is SO much more than that. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525415521ra/25478698.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It is unnerving in the reality of it. This could happen and probably does. I know there are parents out there who are afraid of their children. <br><br>This book made ME afraid of their children.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547915085ra/26942355.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved this book. I added it to my favorites shelf and I haven't done that in LONG time. This disturbed me in such a glorious way. <br><br>I shall be singing its praises for years to come and you best believe I will be picking up anything else Zoje Stage chooses to write!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1517678965ra/24996662.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_2661313957" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2661313957" />
    <a title="Barbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/90413527-barbie"><img alt="Barbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601722083p2/90413527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2661313957?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbie" href="/user/show/90413527-barbie">Barbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36603018-baby-teeth">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2661313957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16405730990598168863"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551534793i/27143282._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b> My thoughts in a nutshell </b><br/>It was way better than I expected. I started with low expectation and I really enjoyed it!<br/><br/><b>The story is about…</b><br/><u>Skip over this point if you don't like the sneak peek. </u><br/>Daddy thinks Hanna is an adorable child. Mommy knows Hanna is a nightmare. Hanna wants daddy and she will be able to do everything for his father even if she has to be a bad girl. She will ruin her mother's life and she doesn't mind it at all. Hanna will enjoy it.<br/><br/><b> What impressed me the most 😊 </b><br/>I love the evil</span>
  <span id="freeText16405730990598168863" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551534793i/27143282._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> My thoughts in a nutshell </b><br>It was way better than I expected. I started with low expectation and I really enjoyed it!<br><br><b>The story is about…</b><br><u>Skip over this point if you don't like the sneak peek. </u><br>Daddy thinks Hanna is an adorable child. Mommy knows Hanna is a nightmare. Hanna wants daddy and she will be able to do everything for his father even if she has to be a bad girl. She will ruin her mother's life and she doesn't mind it at all. Hanna will enjoy it.<br><br><b> What impressed me the most 😊 </b><br>I love the evil child trope. I live for this kind of thriller in a book and the movie. My all-time favorite movie is Orphan. So I felt that I would love this book. <br>It is weird, but I like Hanna as a character. She is mad but the author did a fantastic job with her personalities. I wasn't afraid while I was reading, but Hanna's POV gave me a creepy vibe. When she stood in front of her mother with a hammer and her mother Suzette just creeps out, I thought that <i> 'OK Suzette, you are more insane than your daughter. Just call the police PLS.' </i><br>I see why a lot of people hate this book; because of the characters, especially Hanna's parents. They were irritating. Her father doesn't want to believe that her cute angel is a monster. Firstly, I was pissed about it. Later I accepted it. <br>If Hanna's daddy would have believed immediately that her daughter hurts her mommy then it wouldn't have been a book because that was the whole point. This is a dysfunctional family. Everyone is doing their own things and they aren't communicating. I like the character development. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I think the ending was good. It was the best decision. I agree that they don't allow Hanna to come home. I wouldn't let her come back.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br>I really love the unfinished ending. I would be curious about a second book. <br>The writing style was gripping. I adored that the father was Swedish, and he usually used a Swedish word. It was special. I like that he calls Hanna his lilla gumman.<br><br><b>What I don't like at all ☹️ </b><br> I have a problem with the pacing. I was bored sometimes and to my mind, the book was overwritten. It has some unnecessary scenes. If I cut it off nobody would notice. I don't like that Suzette has Crohn's disease. It was useless. I also don't like when the author collects the problem. Less is sometimes more. Hannah was just enough.<br><br><b> Make a conclusion </b><br>I gave it <b>3 stars </b> because it was entertaining but not perfect. I will <b>round up to 3,5 stars</b> because the author deserves it.<br>This book is not for everyone. You will hate it if you don't like the insane child trope. So I recommend it to readers who love thrillers where the main character is a scary child. <br><b> To be honest, I really want a second book, don't judge me. :D </b><br><br><b> Atmosphere collage </b> aka. <i> how did I imagine the book vibes? </i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552410520i/27194643._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16405730990598168863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2232242170?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2232242170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13077252990269759086">You can also see this review @ <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://readrantrockandroll.com/2018/02/05/baby-teeth-by-zoje-stage-book-review-ngew2018/'>https://readrantrockandroll.com/2018/...</a><br/><br/><b>May contain mild spoilers…</b><br/><br/>Suzette, mother to Hanna, deals with illness on a daily basis. She has an autoimmune disease that makes her sick and causes pain. On top of this, she’s trying to be a good wife to Alex, Hanna’s dad, and all she wants is to have a normal family–a normal daughter. The problem is that Hanna is a complete psycho, doesn’t talk, and behaves so badly, she’s continuously kicked out of school and Suzette has </span>
  <span id="freeText13077252990269759086" style="display:none">You can also see this review @ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://readrantrockandroll.com/2018/02/05/baby-teeth-by-zoje-stage-book-review-ngew2018/">https://readrantrockandroll.com/2018/...</a><br /><br /><b>May contain mild spoilers…</b><br /><br />Suzette, mother to Hanna, deals with illness on a daily basis. She has an autoimmune disease that makes her sick and causes pain. On top of this, she’s trying to be a good wife to Alex, Hanna’s dad, and all she wants is to have a normal family–a normal daughter. The problem is that Hanna is a complete psycho, doesn’t talk, and behaves so badly, she’s continuously kicked out of school and Suzette has no choice but to home school her. At home, there are even more problems. Hanna want’s to kill her mother, but has a deep love for her father and because of that, nobody believes Suzette when she tries to tell them that something is wrong with Hanna.<br /><br /><i>“Daddy was the most handsome man in the world. He dressed nicely, in crisp shirts and colorful ties, and his favorites were the ones she picked our for him. When she grew up she’d marry him, and then Mommy wouldn’t be competition anymore.”</i><br /><br />The main points of view alternate between Suzette and Hanna throughout the book. As I mentioned, Alex, Hanna’s dad, never sees the disturbing behaviors. The person who deals with Hanna on a daily basis is Suzette and this is what made me so uncomfortable throughout the book. Alex refers to Hanna as his ‘squirrely girl’ or ‘lilla gumman’ and it seems like no matter how much he loves Suzette, he just doesn’t believe that his daughter is a psychopath and consistently makes excuses for her. Hanna exhibits aggressive and violent behaviors that almost go too far for me. It made me very uncomfortable and the constant instigating between Hanna and Suzette made me want to scream. This family is extremely dysfunctional and I kept wondering throughout the book what the real reasons for Hanna’s behaviors were. Surely something had to have happened in the past with Suzette or Alex, right?<br /><br /><i>“Sshh, lilla gumman…Daddy’s squirrely girl…”He cooed so softly Suzette couldn’t hear everything he said. But Hanna quieted. She looked so tiny in his arms, a rag doll.</i><br /><br />I thought the book was written really well and it’s certainly a quick and smooth read. People who like thrillers will more than likely be pleased. Personally, I was on edge and completely thrilled all the way to the ‘not so’ surprising end. I was expecting some major twists toward the end which never really came and made me feel like something was missing, however, the book for the most part kept my interest and I found it dark and very disturbing, so for that, I’ll give this book 4****. I’m looking forward to reading more books by this author.<br /><br />Publisher: St. Martin’s Press (July 17, 2018)<br />Language: English<br />ISBN-10: 1250170753<br />ISBN-13: 978-1250170750</span>
  <a data-text-id="13077252990269759086" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2270550273" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2270550273" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2270550273?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5032725-debra?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2270550273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11643605086684022335">Baby Teeth is a "psychological" thriller focusing on a dysfunctional family and their child with disturbing behavior. Alex, the father, does not want to see or believe that his daughter has behavioral/emotional problems. His daughter behaves around him, she is loving and, although she does not speak, she has her own way of communicating with him. Suzette, the Mother, is homeschooling her daughter while dealing with the symptoms of her Crohn's disease. Suzette is the target or her daughter, Hanna</span>
  <span id="freeText11643605086684022335" style="display:none">Baby Teeth is a "psychological" thriller focusing on a dysfunctional family and their child with disturbing behavior. Alex, the father, does not want to see or believe that his daughter has behavioral/emotional problems. His daughter behaves around him, she is loving and, although she does not speak, she has her own way of communicating with him. Suzette, the Mother, is homeschooling her daughter while dealing with the symptoms of her Crohn's disease. Suzette is the target or her daughter, Hanna’s, "bad" behaviors. Hanna begins to speak to her Mother and really wants her father all to herself. She is clever, manipulative, and unwilling to speak. She does not like going to traditional schools and engages in behaviors which result in her leaving the traditional school environment.<br /><br />This book is told through POV chapters titled "Suzette" or "Hanna” The reader gets a glimpse into the mind of each. Hanna is the proverbial "bad" seed who acts out and has behaviors which get her into all kinds of trouble. Although she is seven years old, she had thoughts and actions, I would associate with a much older child. While reading the book, I kept waiting for the light bulb to go off over Alex's head and for him to finally "see the light". Suzette, being the target of most of her daughter's bad behaviors, struggles with feelings ranging from wanting to help her daughter, fearing her child, and wanting to not have to deal with her child anymore.<br /><br />For me this book was a solid 3 stars. I thought of the movie, "The Good Son" while reading this book. Hanna has "evil" thoughts and is perhaps mentally ill. I won’t say more about the family or their family dynamic. Hanna is creepy, and this book is a fast read but most of the actions felt "gratuitous" and there for shock value to move the story along. There are a lot of negative behaviors, actions and thoughts in this book that it almost became too much. As characters spiraled out of control, the pace picked up but again things just felt gratuitous. Some may also be turned off by the way Suzette speaks to her child. I get that the Author is trying to show how frustrated Suzette is with her child and how Hanna has pushed Suzette to the breaking point. Still, it may not sit well with some. I would describe this book as good not great. For me there was something missing. Initially I really enjoyed the book but as I read more, I felt a disconnect but still wanted to know how the book was going to end. There was a battle going on and I wanted to see who won - even though no one really wins in these situations.<br /><br />I am curious to see what future books this Author writes.<br /><br />I received a copy of this book from St. Martin's Press and NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />See more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.openbookpost.com">www.openbookpost.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11643605086684022335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2268564926" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2268564926" />
    <a title="Berit☀️✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38946743-berit"><img alt="Berit☀️✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534383878p2/38946743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2268564926?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Berit☀️✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Berit☀️✨" href="/user/show/38946743-berit">Berit☀️✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38946743-berit?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38946743-berit?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2268564926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer418222640618495393"><b>4 controversial stars🌟🌟🌟🌟</b><br/><br/>*** I am updating my rating to a solid 4 Stars for the following reasons....<br/>• I read this book in February and it has stayed with me over the last six months and as much as I read that absolutely says something!<br/>• I allowed other peoples opinions to sway my own when it came to this book, and that was not fair to the book or to the author!<br/>*** I still stand by every word in my review, this was a very compelling and engaging read for ME!<br/><br/>I believe I’m going to bust out my com</span>
  <span id="freeText418222640618495393" style="display:none"><b>4 controversial stars🌟🌟🌟🌟</b><br /><br />*** I am updating my rating to a solid 4 Stars for the following reasons....<br />• I read this book in February and it has stayed with me over the last six months and as much as I read that absolutely says something!<br />• I allowed other peoples opinions to sway my own when it came to this book, and that was not fair to the book or to the author!<br />*** I still stand by every word in my review, this was a very compelling and engaging read for ME!<br /><br />I believe I’m going to bust out my complement sandwich for this review... as a refresher a complement sandwich is good/bad/good.... so in short the bad is sandwiched in between the good..... I also want to make it very clear that I read this with a group and I was in the true minority on this.... so the opinions in this review are absolutely my own and my review should be read with the understanding that this book is unquestionably not for everybody....<br /><br />This book is about Hannah a seven-year-old who has some pretty major issues.... one of them being the fact that she wants to get rid of her mother.... for good....Suzette is an exhausted mother at the end of her rope, what has she done to deserve this child? As a mother I would love to believe that I would do all the right things in this situation, but next to Hana my children are absolute perfection (just don’t tell them that)..... I felt the author did a good job in the portrayal of the parents the overly stressed out mother and the oblivious father.... and the tension this would put on a relationship when Dad chooses to pretend that daughter is perfectly normal and mom wants to pull her hair out....<br /><br />Now to the meat of the sandwich, the problems I had with this book.... hannah’s age was probably my biggest problem, I just found it very unbelievable that a child of her age was able to have the thought process and knowledge that she did no matter how gifted she was..... this I believe leads to the real problem if Hannah were 12(The age I believe A character who acted as she did was more apt to be) then she probably would have already been diagnosed and been in some major therapy.... however this also begs the question why was she not in major therapy at seven? Perhaps Alex and Suzette were not parents of the year, but they did take her to see several doctors and I’m not quite sure why more wasn’t done at a younger age? Although if something were done at a younger age we would not have had this book.... so perhaps that is the reason....<br /><br />This was a quick page turning red that probably would be better classified as horror..... and if this is a genre you stay away from I’d definitely recommend staying away from this book.... this is a book that you can’t say you liked it, but I will say I appreciated it.... it definitely made me think, what would I do if I were this mother? And I believe sometimes it is hard not to judge in this situation, but I am a firm believer that unless you have walked in somebody’s shoes you really have no idea what is going on in their life and that’s kind of how I looked at this book....<br /><br />So I’m going to take the easy way out and neither recommend this book or not recommend this book.... I’m going to leave it up to you, because this book evoked some pretty seriously strong reactions in people.... so if you choose to read it, read it knowing there is some disturbing content and it is 100% not for everybody....<br /><br />*** thank you to the publisher and Net Galley for a copy of this book ***</span>

<div id="review_2272182372" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2272182372" />
    <a title="Tammy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50603889-tammy"><img alt="Tammy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566220700p2/50603889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2272182372?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammy" href="/user/show/50603889-tammy">Tammy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2272182372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3646533881269533021">Is it possible for a child to be a psychopath? Is aberrant behavior the result of nature or nuture ? These are questions I’ll leave to minds far better than mine. This is a deeply unsettling novel about the proverbial bad seed. It is told from the alternating points of view of the mother and child. Hanna is seven years old and silent which make her thoughts and consuming love for her father all the more chilling. Manipulative and malicious, Hanna has one goal and it isn’t pretty. We are talking </span>
  <span id="freeText3646533881269533021" style="display:none">Is it possible for a child to be a psychopath? Is aberrant behavior the result of nature or nuture ? These are questions I’ll leave to minds far better than mine. This is a deeply unsettling novel about the proverbial bad seed. It is told from the alternating points of view of the mother and child. Hanna is seven years old and silent which make her thoughts and consuming love for her father all the more chilling. Manipulative and malicious, Hanna has one goal and it isn’t pretty. We are talking about one very twisted sister here. On occasion I felt empathy for Hanna until she acted out in ways that were unimaginable. Child from hell aside, this book is also about the perfect facade of a dysfunctional family and the sinister telling of mangled psyches. Pathological behavior has to come from somewhere, doesn’t it? And the ending? I’m not going to tell you about that.</span>
