<div id="review_2229615887" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2229615887" />
    <a title="Taryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1334938-taryn"><img alt="Taryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407768387p2/1334938.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2229615887?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taryn" href="/user/show/1334938-taryn">Taryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1334938-taryn?shelf=top-to-read">top-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1334938-taryn?shelf=received-from-publisher">received-from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1334938-taryn?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2229615887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17462976380826259071"><blockquote>
  <em>"There’s nothing scarier than loving a child and not understanding what they’re trying to tell you—”</em>
</blockquote><br/><br/>There's not enough room in the house for both Hanna and her Mommy! Seven-year-old Hanna would be so much happier if Mommy would just disappear so that she and her Daddy could live happily ever after. <strong>Through Hanna and Suzette's (Mommy) eyes, we see their daily battles to maintain control in an unpredictable, ever-changing world and what it's like to maneuver through life when no one will hear </strong></span>
  <span id="freeText17462976380826259071" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <em>"There’s nothing scarier than loving a child and not understanding what they’re trying to tell you—”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />There's not enough room in the house for both Hanna and her Mommy! Seven-year-old Hanna would be so much happier if Mommy would just disappear so that she and her Daddy could live happily ever after. <strong>Through Hanna and Suzette's (Mommy) eyes, we see their daily battles to maintain control in an unpredictable, ever-changing world and what it's like to maneuver through life when no one will hear you. </strong>The people in this story are permanently tied together by blood, but have toxic effects on each other. (<strong>Warning:</strong> After the ARC disclaimer, I get a little spoilery talking about a part of the book that came up in my comment section, though I don't really consider it a true spoiler. The content may be upsetting for some.)<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>It was hard to pour endless love into someone who wouldn’t love you back. No one could do it forever.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />Yet another book for the "What the heck is wrong with me?" pile! I want to emphasize that I say that in jest! I don't actually think there is anything wrong with anyone who reads this book, whether they like it or not. I don't even think it's the most scandalous book to sweep through the Goodreads community (or middle school hallways lol)! However, it's horrific, creepy, and disturbing. I have always found value in disturbing stories. Sometimes it can make us more empathetic. Reading uncomfortable material has helped me avoid danger by exposing me to a wide range of situations and people I couldn't have possibly experienced myself. Sometimes it's more effective or "safer" to explore difficult concepts from a distance or through the filter of absurdity. I think disturbing books have less value to those who have close experience with the topics being addressed. There are certain topics I avoid completely or can only handle in certain formats (fiction over nonfiction, written over visual). <strong>This book will not be for everyone. Know your limits!</strong><br /><br /><em>Baby Teeth</em> is exactly what I expected from reading the description. I'm totally fascinated by terrifying kids: <em>The Bad Seed</em>, <em>The Good Son</em>, even Stewie Griffin from <em>Family Guy</em>! Hanna is a true terror. I live for the "Whaaaaaaat?" moments in horror and she certainly provided plenty of those. I questioned some of Hanna's actions due to her age, but the whole story is so over-the-top that I just accepted it within the context of the story.<strong> The controversy comes from Hanna's murderous antics and Suzette treating Hanna like an enemy combatant.</strong> I'll leave Hanna's shocking actions for you to discover, but there's actually a ton to analyze beyond her constantly escalating behavior!<br /><br /><u>
  <strong>THE CHARACTERS</strong>
</u><br />• Suzette/Mommy - "Too many things in her life were tinged with horror." Suzette has suffered from unpredictable Crohn's Disease since she was a teenager. <strong>Not only is Suzette’s own body attacking her, but she’s being attacked by her own child. </strong>Motherhood is not measuring up to her expectations. She told herself she would never be like her own inattentive mother, but she's completely blindsided when she's dealt a different version of the same hand.<br />• <strong>Hanna's parents can tick all the boxes on a “Signs that Your Kid Might Be a Sociopath” list.</strong> As creepy and devious as Hanna is, I actually developed a soft spot for her! She senses that her mom resents her and has a deep fear of abandonment. Even though many of her perceptions are unfounded, it's all very real to her. She's always reading the behavior of the adults around her, but it's through the distorted lens of her own limited experience. To be fair, the adults aren't so good at reading things either!<br />• <strong>Alex/Daddy is in deep denial. He refuses to listen to his wife or any professional who dares to insinuate that Hanna is anything less than perfect.</strong> There's never direct evidence of her worst offenses and he dismisses the minor behavioral problems as the boredom of an extremely intelligent child. His peacekeeping attempts fuel the conflict between mother and daughter.<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>THE THEMES:</u>
</strong><br /><br /><u>
  <strong>Body Horror<br /></strong>
</u>• Suzette's body has betrayed her repeatedly. She is under a doctor's care, but she's constantly worried about the next flare-up. When Suzette becomes pregnant she felt a loss of self. It's like an alien overtook her body! Pregnancy caused her to lose control of her body because she wasn't able to take her medications.<br />• Hanna expresses discomfort at the idea of her baby teeth falling out. I think aging—and the separation that comes with it—causes distress for her. She also notices Suzette's preoccupation with appearances and it colors the way she sees the world. She frequently attacks Suzette in ways that will disfigure her, in hopes that Daddy will see Suzette the way she does. She thinks if Suzette is unattractive, Daddy will finally see the light and leave.<strong>
  <br />
</strong><br /><br /><u>
  <strong>Masks/Facades/Costumes</strong>
</u><br />• Hanna frequently describes seeing her Mommy's masks: Good Mommy and Bad Mommy. Everything is black-and-white in her seven-year-old mind and there's no room for complexity. In her mind, Bad Mommy is the real one. Daddy is the consistent parent who loves her unconditionally. Hanna panics when adults put on unexpected masks or act weird because it makes her feel a loss of control.<br />• Alex's denial of Hanna's behavioral issues is a costume of sorts.<br />• Born bad? Interestingly enough, Hanna has to conjure up a demonic pal to help her with her worst acts. Hanna feels more comfortable putting herself out there when her friend around. (Hanna's imaginary pal was a <strong>victim of self-preservation and other peoples' misinterpretations of the world around them.</strong>)<br /><br /><blockquote><em>She didn’t like that they were both focused on her; their misguided expectations formed a black hole in her gut. Black holes were dangerous; they absorbed everything around them, and maybe some parts of her that she needed would tumble into the abyss. </em>(Hanna)</blockquote><br /><br /><u>
  <strong>Perfection/Desire for Control</strong>
</u><br />• Suzette's life and body are in constant turmoil, so it's important that she takes care of the things she does have control over. She's obsessed with keeping a sterile house and making sure her family appears well taken care of. She finds comfort in completing mindless tasks. Suzette is tormented by her physical scars and she's terrified that she'll have to get an ileostomy bag.  She thinks that if she lets herself go, Alex might leave her.<br />• Because of Hanna's need for control, she finds comfort in solitude and math. Hanna knows she's different and not in a good way: "She knew what adults liked and didn’t like: rabbit-like girls who kept still and never raised their voice were good; dragon-like girls who roared and stomped and flew and generated their own fire were bad."  Mommy notices Hanna's failings the most, so she faces the full brunt of Hanna's wrath.<em> </em>The pressure to be something she's not is too much for Hanna. A fear of failure stunts her growth (refusal to talk, refusal to draw). She's terrified of going to school and freaks out at the mention of it. She's drawn to ugly stuffed creatures, relieved to have a friend that is "ugly, broken."<br /><br /><blockquote><em>A vengeful pit grew inside her and it remained to be seen how it would grow—very possibly into a tree with snaking branches and claws. How fun it would be to be such a tree, looming like a giant on a neighborhood street. People would pass beneath her, and the ones she didn’t like—snap snap crunch! She’d snatch them up and tangle her branches around them, and their bones would break with little crunches that would be mistaken for the snap of a twig. Her bark-self would absorb their yummy blood and the tree would grow and thrive. </em>(Hanna)</blockquote><br /><br /><u><strong>Communication/Inability to Communicate</strong>:</u><br />• Suzette's mother's inattention to Suzette's pain had disastrous consequences for Suzette. When Suzette met Alex, she finally found someone who would listen to her. But when it comes to Hanna, he's completely blind. He gets to be the fun parent, while Suzette has to deal with a defiant child and day-to-day child rearing. Now, it's Alex who's not listening to her. She's ashamed that her own child is rejecting her and is beginning to question her own perceptions. Throughout the story, she’s drawn to authoritative adults who take the time to listen to her and offer to help her take control of the situation.<br />• Hanna doesn't talk, but she has a vivid imagination. She's frustrated that words don't come out the way she intends. She hears her parents in the bedroom and is upset at this "language" that excludes her. She tried to communicate with them by grunting, but they STILL don't understand her. Hanna experiences overwhelming relief when she meets a person who finally finds a way to communicate with her effectively and takes the time to understand her.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>Hanna would sit there, watching them, trying to decipher the puffs of smoke. How much had her young brain already misconstrued? Observing, absorbing. Warping, twisting. Drawing conclusions about everything they did.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><u>
  <strong>THE BIG ONE: How perceptive young children are and how they process the world around them.</strong>
</u><br />• There's a constant battle of wills between Suzette and Hanna, but they actually have a lot in common.<strong> In some ways, Suzette and Hanna's relationship seems like a continuation of Suzette's fraught relationship with her own mother.</strong> Suzette's mother was completely unmindful of the psychological and physical damage she was inflicting on Suzette. Like Hanna, Suzette was constantly disappointed by her mother and she wanted her mother to prove herself worthy of her love. Even when she was pushing her mother away, it was important to her that her mother make an effort to reach out: "It was a child’s selfish desire, but mothers were meant to be selfless."<br />• The pivotal moment in Hannah and Suzette's relationship is when Suzette is inappropriately candid with two-year-old Hanna. She doesn't consider how much Hanna can understand or how a young child with limited experience might process the information. It's a frustrating scene to witness, because of <strong>all the miscommunications that ignite the toxic cycle of Hanna and Suzette's relationship</strong>: Hannah is stressed out because Mommy is acting weird→Hanna tries to get her Mommy's attention the only way a two-year-old can→ Suzette interprets it as yet another one of her maternal failings, when Hanna is actually just being a normal toddler→The situation spirals out of control.<br /><br /><u>
  <strong>CONCLUSION</strong>
</u><br /><br />This is the story of mothers, daughters and the unmet expectations between them. Both Hanna and Suzette struggle with feelings of exclusion and fears of abandonment. Their similarities widen the gap between them. Was Hanna born sick or did her parents exacerbate the situation? Could this be the explosive reaction of nature and nurture? I didn't see any answers, but <b>I couldn't help but wonder if Hanna would've turned out a tad different if her parents were better equipped to handle her.</b><br /><br />Making me soften towards Hanna and harden towards Suzette was quite the authorial feat! <strong>I really liked this book because there was a lot to analyze and the characters are memorable. It reminded me to be careful when I talk in front of children because they are listening to every word!</strong><strong> </strong><strong>This book isn't for everyone and it's NOT uplifting!</strong> Recommended if you're in the mood to read about a fictional family's trainwreck of a life! :)<br /><br /><strong>_____________<br />I received this book for free from NetGalley and St. Martin's Press. This does not affect my opinion of the book or the content of my review. It will be available on July 17, 2018!</strong><br /><br />Since my morals were questioned due to my liking this book, I want to be very clear about what I liked and why some parts didn't shock me enough to ruin the book for me. Below I summarize one of the parts causing controversy and how I read it. It's just one more thing on the pile of things Hanna does, so it mostly just spoils the shock. Proceed at your own risk. It might be upsetting or spoilery to some.<br /><br /><strong>..............................................SPOILER TIME!---</strong><br />I hesitate to say that the following are the most disturbing scenes in the book because Hanna gets more determined and violent as the story goes on. However, the upsetting part for many readers occurs around 40%: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Hanna's parents think she's asleep, but she's actually lurking around the house. She spots her parents being intimate on the couch. She has NO boundaries and doesn't run off in horror and denial like the average child (<a href="https://www.buzzfeed.com/kaylayandoli/never-playing-hide-and-seek-again?utm_term=.skzgqaxzz#.snPPa1p55" rel="nofollow noopener">although apparently there are even weirder reactions to have</a>). Instead, she stays and watches for a bit. She sees the scene before her through the lens of her own experiences. She sees it as a violent act ("savagery"). This could be the moment that Daddy is finally getting rid of Mommy! She realizes that's not what's happening at all. Daddy is actually being bewitched by Mommy; this is obviously all part of Mommy's plan to win over Daddy and get rid of Hanna for good. There's no room for Hanna in this situation. She creeps back to bed without anyone hearing her. Later on, she imitates what she saw and comes up with a SERIOUSLY DISTURBING story to freak out her mother. Suzette freaks out.  (That last part did shock me, especially the language she used. The childish naïveté of previous chapters evaporated.)<br /><br /><strong>This book deals with careless adults and how kids are influenced by the things they see and overhear.</strong>  I <strong>DON'T</strong> think the scene Hanna witnessed was appropriate for her to see. Nothing in the story indicates Alex and Suzette think that it would be an appropriate thing for Hanna to see. They didn't know she was there, but they should've been more careful. However, I<strong> don't</strong> think she's the first child to walk in on her parents. I <strong>don't</strong> think it's unusual for a curious, intelligent child to be interested in adult matters. I'll out myself as a former weirdo kid: I used to hide behind the couch while my mom watched soap operas and then later reenact scenes with my Babysitter's Club dolls. When I was Hanna's age, I wrote an "encyclopedia" of topics that I thought kids needed to be aware of. <a href="http://theoverlyattachedreader.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/02/weirdkid.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">This is the book cover</a>. Obviously, I was paying more attention to the evening news than my parents realized! I <strong>don't</strong> remember the elementary school playground being an especially angelic place, in part because of the influences of older siblings, television, adults being comfortable around the house, etc. <strong>Hanna is an extreme version of this.</strong> In her case, Suzette uses inappropriate language with her and her internet access isn't heavily monitored. One of the main characters is a child, but I <strong>don't</strong> think this is a book for children. Not going to lie though; I would've totally snuck it into my library pile as a teenager! <strong>I'm not an authority on how other people will react to this book.</strong> I can only speak to my own reaction. My interpretations may be completely off-base! You can probably find books with similar themes without the shocking plot points. I <strong>do</strong> understand how the scenes can be seen as offensive. I have my own lines I won't cross. In terms of context and the demographic it's being marketed to, it just didn't affect me that strongly. I don't think there's anything wrong with that.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2275722402" />
    <a title="Kaceey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13442817-kaceey"><img alt="Kaceey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463899458p2/13442817.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2275722402?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaceey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaceey" href="/user/show/13442817-kaceey">Kaceey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36603018-baby-teeth">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13442817-kaceey?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2275722402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14046847165338631544"><b>2.5*</b><br/>Tough call on this one. Enjoyed the author - well written. With that said, the over-the-top subject matter was so shocking to me it was difficult to keep my perspective. For that reason alone, it just wasn’t for me. <b>Though I'm definitely in the minority here.</b> <br/><br/><i>Mothers are daughters....</i><br/><br/>Hanna is 7 years old and Daddy’s little girl. Her world revolves around her love for dear daddy.<br/>Now her mother...well, that’s another matter. If only mommy wasn’t around...if only she didn’t have to share daddy </span>
  <span id="freeText14046847165338631544" style="display:none"><b>2.5*</b><br />Tough call on this one. Enjoyed the author - well written. With that said, the over-the-top subject matter was so shocking to me it was difficult to keep my perspective. For that reason alone, it just wasn’t for me. <b>Though I'm definitely in the minority here.</b> <br /><br /><i>Mothers are daughters....</i><br /><br />Hanna is 7 years old and Daddy’s little girl. Her world revolves around her love for dear daddy.<br />Now her mother...well, that’s another matter. If only mommy wasn’t around...if only she didn’t have to share daddy with <i>her.</i> <br /><br />Suzette loves her husband more than anything in this world. They have a daughter, Hanna, who she desperately wants to love too. But she just can’t get there. No connection or bond whatsoever. No, this isn’t just your typical riff between a parent and a teenager. Hanna is only seven. So who’s to blame for this total disconnect? Sweet little Hanna, or emotionally exhausted Suzette? <br /><br />As the hurtful acts between mother and daughter escalate, reading this book became more difficult. So hard to imagine <b>a seven year old child</b> plotting and carrying out the despicable acts that she committed. It was really just too dark and depressing for me. (Even though my inner-voice kept trying to remind me…it’s just a book!) Perhaps if the child was portrayed as older, capable of higher level of thought it might have been more palatable for me. <br /><br />Many other readers and reviewers really enjoyed this book, so I hope if you do pick it up, it works for you too!!<br /><br />Thank you to NetGalley, St Martin’s Press and Zoje Stage for an ARC to review in exchange for an honest review.</span>

<div id="review_3413308757" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3413308757" />
    <a title="Larry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/108612357-larry"><img alt="Larry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579224313p2/108612357.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_2353560131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2353560131" />
    <a title="Theresa Alan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3268839-theresa-alan"><img alt="Theresa Alan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1265739602p2/3268839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2353560131?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Theresa Alan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Theresa Alan" href="/user/show/3268839-theresa-alan">Theresa Alan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2353560131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17060051519746677991">This novel is described as a thriller. I think it would be better categorized as horror. It’s told from the point of view of an exasperated stay-at-home mom, Suzette, and her seven-year=old daughter, Hannah. Hannah refuses to speak. When Dad is home, she is smiley and delightful. When he’s at work, she does her best to make her mom’s life a living hell. When Suzette tries to enroll her first in preschool, then kindergarten, then first grade, Hannah snarls at teachers and starts fires and hurts o</span>
  <span id="freeText17060051519746677991" style="display:none">This novel is described as a thriller. I think it would be better categorized as horror. It’s told from the point of view of an exasperated stay-at-home mom, Suzette, and her seven-year=old daughter, Hannah. Hannah refuses to speak. When Dad is home, she is smiley and delightful. When he’s at work, she does her best to make her mom’s life a living hell. When Suzette tries to enroll her first in preschool, then kindergarten, then first grade, Hannah snarls at teachers and starts fires and hurts other children. Suzette has no choice but to do her best to home school her. She has battled debilitating health issues of her own since high school and having this out-of-control child is not helping her physical or mental health.<br /><br />This is not a fun read. It’s gripping, but it’s really hard for me to imagine a child who hates her mother so much. I’ve read stories of kids who are physically and emotionally abused by a parent, and still the kid professes love for his or her parent. So to have a child so young purposely trying to do anything she can to destroy a non-abusive mother is extremely foreign to me. <br /><br />This book is well written. It’s a tense, disturbing read. So, if you’re in the mood for that, you might enjoy this. <br /><br />Thanks so much to NetGalley and St. Martin’s Press for the opportunity to review this novel, which RELEASES JULY 17, 2018.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17060051519746677991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18335273793253680152">Boy you can bet I am glad to see the back of this baby. Teeth or no.<br/><br/>Not going to lie I did not care for this at all. <br/><br/>For those of you who do not know, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35410511.Baby_Teeth' title='Baby Teeth by Zoje Stage' rel='nofollow noopener'>Baby Teeth</a> is the story of Hanna, a little girl who is determined to kill her mother. <br/><br/>Of course any story of this nature is going to be an uncomfortable read and I was very aware of that hurdle from the onset.   <span id="freeText18335273793253680152" style="display:none">Boy you can bet I am glad to see the back of this baby. Teeth or no.<br /><br />Not going to lie I did not care for this at all. <br /><br />For those of you who do not know, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35410511.Baby_Teeth" title="Baby Teeth by Zoje Stage" rel="nofollow noopener">Baby Teeth</a> is the story of Hanna, a little girl who is determined to kill her mother. <br /><br />Of course any story of this nature is going to be an uncomfortable read and I was very aware of that hurdle from the onset. That said, no doubt I would have found this more unsettling than I did, had I bought into any of it. I did not. <br /><br />The story is told through two perspectives; that of Hanna, the little girl and her mother Suzette. From the very beginning I had a difficult time connecting with these voices. They did not ring true for me.<br /><br />I never found that what was happening on the page felt real, no tension, no drama.<br /><br />It all seemed too contrived, too bent on shocking and horrifying the reader in as many gratuitous ways as possible. <br /><br />Sorry folks but for me this was a shallow basin.<br /><br />As always my thanks to St. Martin’s Press, NetGalley and Zoje Stage for an opportunity to read and review this book. :)</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2277067491" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2277067491" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2277067491?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Matt by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/8843732-heidi-lynn-s-bookreviews">Heidi Lynn’s BookReviews</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=equinox-book-challenge">equinox-book-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2277067491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11287502103784204616">First and foremost, a large thank you to NetGalley, Zoje Stage, and St. Martin’s Press for providing me with a copy of this publication, which allows me to provide you with an unbiased review.<br/><br/>In her debut novel, Zoje Stage has made quite a name for herself. Exploring some dark and disturbing areas of the parent-child relationship, the reader is forced to see a seemingly calm little girl turn against her own mother. Hanna Jensen appears to be quite the average four-year-old girl, with one glaring</span>
  <span id="freeText11287502103784204616" style="display:none">First and foremost, a large thank you to NetGalley, Zoje Stage, and St. Martin’s Press for providing me with a copy of this publication, which allows me to provide you with an unbiased review.<br /><br />In her debut novel, Zoje Stage has made quite a name for herself. Exploring some dark and disturbing areas of the parent-child relationship, the reader is forced to see a seemingly calm little girl turn against her own mother. Hanna Jensen appears to be quite the average four-year-old girl, with one glaring exception; she does not speak and never has. Countless tests and examinations have left her parents, Alex and Suzette, baffled, as there is nothing physical wrong with her. With her muteness comes the added issue that she is unable to acclimate into any scholastic situation, leaving Suzette to homeschool Hanna. While there is no verbal communication, Hanna’s comprehension and written word is advanced for her young age. What no one has been able to see is that Hanna has another side, a darker side that is focussed on tearing Suzette down in a well-planned manner. Hanna internalises her struggle, but is happy to show her mother an evil side and purposely sabotage any progress that is being made. What begins as simple defecating on the floor turns to barking and, eventually, full-on violence in a school setting. While Suzette tries to come to terms with this, Alex is oblivious and sees only the princess-like girl that Hanna presents on a nightly basis. After Hanna tips her hand and shows off an alter-ego, Suzette is no longer prepared to go at this alone, but Alex remains uncertain that Hanna is to blame for anything. Hanna sets out her own plan to get rid of Suzette once and for all, allowing her to have Alex’s attention forevermore. While Suzette knows it is coming, she is helpless to slay the monster before her, seeing it has taken the form of sweet Hanna Jensen. Stage weaves together quite the disturbing tale here, pitting parental instinct against base survival. Fans who enjoy a diluted psychological thriller may enjoy this one, as its presentation has rounded edges and light spine tingles.<br /><br />When this novel was recommended to me by a friend, I wanted to give it my full attention, not only because of its subject matter, but also because it would fit perfectly into a reading challenge requirement. It would seem that Stage has found herself with a great deal of Goodreads activity where reviews continue to grow on both sides of the fence. I can see where both the five- and one-star folks are coming from, having been able to situate myself somewhere in the middle. The characters found herein are perfectly crafted and complement one another so well. Hanna is that young child who has a love of her father and inherent dislike of her mother, partially because there is a need to share, but also due to the fact that Suzette is her primary caregiver. Hanna manifests her dislike from disobedience through to full plotting of injury and death of the woman who has nothing but confused love for her. As the story progresses, Hanna’s character turns darker, especially with the revelation of an alter-ego, though things always bounce back when Alex is in the room, which only perpetuates the tug-of-war between the parental units. Suzette, on the other hand, is a woman who has suffered much medical and emotional turmoil in her life and has had to wrestle with a mother of her own who could not care about her. Suzette seeks to be a better mother and person, but Hanna seems to bring out the worst and they battle regularly. While Suzette may seem the paranoid one, her significant time and experiences with Hanna fuels this push to have her daughter examined by professionals, while Alex seeks to protect his offspring. Many of the secondary characters work well here, especially in peeling back the onion and seeing just how destructive Hanna can be, even if her father refuses to see it. The story itself is well-done, choosing to alternate chapters from the perspective of Hanna and Suzette. One could see where things were going, but it was a matter of how swiftly they would get there and how outlandish things could get by the end. Where I struggled with this novel was the intensity level. True, not all books have to have “psychopathic serial killers” to be successful, but I felt Stage wanted to unveil the truly demonic side of Hanna on a regular basis, but diluted it for reasons unknown. I wanted to be shocked and feel Suzette’s pain, but it almost seemed as though some of the narrative chose to gloss over things, lessening the impact. Still, for a debut novel, Stage kept me curious, especially with the ongoing symbolism that the attentive reader will gather as they forge ahead in this piece. Well constructed and I would surely give Zoje Stage another try, hoping that she and her publisher take some of the criticisms that are coming out, to heart.<br /><br />Kudos, Madam Stage, for this very interesting debut. I can see much potential within the genre and hope you’ll keep writing. Your fan base is sure to grow exponentially, especially with all the popularity this book is receiving online.<br /><br />This book fulfils Topic #4 (Title/Author Beginning with Q, X, or Z) of the A Book for All Seasons (Equinox #2) Book Challenge.<br /><br />Like/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br />A Book for All Seasons, a different sort of Book Challenge: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/248185-a-book-for-all-seasons">https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11287502103784204616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

</a><br/><br/>In all seriousness, when I made a placeholder <b>This Is America, I Want It Now</b> “review” it was more like me channeling my inner Oprah and putting this out into the universe à la The Secret in hopes of winning the Goodreads Giveaway. When I received an e-mail from St. Martin’</span>
  <span id="freeText9179283030562097425" style="display:none"><b>FLOAT BECAUSE IT'S THIS BABY'S BERFDAY!!!!!</b><br><br>Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>This book doesn’t come out until Summer of 2018, which really sucks - - - FOR ALL OF YOU!!!! Did you fall for that?????<br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515003859ra/24824132.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>In all seriousness, when I made a placeholder <b>This Is America, I Want It Now</b> “review” it was more like me channeling my inner Oprah and putting this out into the universe à la The Secret in hopes of winning the Goodreads Giveaway. When I received an e-mail from St. Martin’s Press offering me an advanced copy …. well, y’all probably heard me screaming across the entire planet. Then when it came I did <s>really assholey</s> super nice things like <s>rub it in my friend’s face</s> share my joy . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515003859i/24824133._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Mitchell was happy to see me take a leap off the porn wagon and had much excite about our potentially stabby windfall as well . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515003859i/24824134._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I was so excited I didn’t even remember to update my status that I was reading it. Since I never put it down until I was finished, there wasn’t much point. *shrug*<br><br>Being as <i>Baby Teeth</i> doesn’t come out for another seven months, I’m a little hamstrung when it comes to doing much more than singing its praises. To be honest, I’m not even sure if I’m supposed to be posting a review, but since I didn’t receive any blatant instructions <b>not</b> to, I will wait for my cease and desist letter before taking this down : )<br><br>The synopsis here is straightforward. Hanna loves Daddy. Hanna <b>does not</b> love Mommy. In fact, things would be perfect if Mommy wasn’t in the picture at all.<br><br>Now, before you even start naysaying about how this story has been told before I need you to kindly STFU. Even Mark Twain said, “There is no such thing as a new idea. It is impossible. We simply take a lot of old ideas and put them into a sort of mental kaleidoscope. We give them a turn and they make new and curious combinations. We keep on turning and making new combinations indefinitely; but they are the same old pieces of colored glass that have been in use through all the ages.” So yes, simply put this story has been told before . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515003859ra/24824135.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And before that . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515003859ra/24824136.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And even before that back in the olde days of yore by a dude named Longfellow . . . . <br><br>“There was a little girl,<br> Who had a little curl,<br>Right in the middle of her forehead.<br>When she was good,<br>She was very good indeed,<br>But when she was bad she was horrid.”<br><br>I’m telling you it doesn’t matter. Obviously if you didn’t like any of <i>those</i> stories you should probably save your dollars and refrain from buying this one. Zoje Stage is quite the wordsmith, but I don’t think she has a magic wand that will make you like things you normally hate . . . (But maybe Marie-Anne does????) If you <i>did</i> enjoy those others, <i>Baby Teeth</i> will be a sure winner. And there <b>is</b> a fresh take here because Hanna isn’t a cookie cutter of those other children. Neither is her mother. I’d love to say more, but I’m pretty sure my next communication from St. Martin’s Press would go a little summin like . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515003859ra/24824137.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What I am going to do is <s>break</s> BEND (just bending please don’t send me that cease and desist) the rules and give you just a taste of an edited snippet in order to hopefully not piss off the powers that be of what <i>Baby Teeth</i> has to offer (and please remember, that I did receive an ARC, so this may change – but I hope it doesn’t) . . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>Hanna giggled and kept writing. When she was ready, she held up her masterpiece.<br><br>‘Fuck Mommy. She is week and stupid.’<br><br>“… By the way, you used the wrong spelling – it’s w-e-A-k.”</i>
</b><br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515003859ra/24824138.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>One final note: You may be wondering why I haven’t talked about “Daddy” more. Here’s what I have to say to him . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515003859ra/24824139.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I’m going to go ahead and leave it at that before all the words start shooting out of my fingers. I’ll be <s>breaking</s> BENDING – JUST BENDING my own rule come summertime-summertime-sum-sum-summertime and floating this review in order to make sure it is on everyone’s radar. Then all you fellow weirdos have to go get a copy, read it and come back so we can talk about Hanna and Mommy under spoilsie code because I have sooooooo many things I want to barf out all over here about my thoughts and feelz. <br><br><i>Endless thanks goes to Jordan at St. Martin’s Press for this opportunity. I don’t know how a debut author convinces a major publishing house to go all in like it appears you guys are doing for this little story, but I think you hit the jackpot. Congrats in advance, you picked a good ‘un.</i><br><br><b>ORIGINAL "REVIEW:"</b><br><br>Have you <b>SEEN</b> this synopsis?????<br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1513352410ra/24683673.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Dear Zoje Stage: This is America, I want it now ; ) <br><br>#thewaitwillkillme</span>

  <span id="freeText5129072962341843938" style="display:none">Hello Readers!<br /><br />As more reader reviews are coming in it's becoming apparent that BABY TEETH elicits strong reactions from some people, and a lot of debate. <div id="review_2191580916" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2191580916" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60039400-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549124309p2/60039400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2191580916?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/60039400-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2191580916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14206487596331963052">Okay okay okay... Let me ask you this. Do you have kids? Has your child ever freaked out in a restaurant or in a store? If you don’t have kids I bet you’ve thought “lady, get this kid out of here!” And I do! Because 👏🏼 mama 👏🏼 don’t 👏🏼 play 👏🏼! Now, a little tantrum every now and then is normal (believe me, my 5 year old still speaks whinese 🙄) BUT in Baby Teeth by Zoje Stage you get way more than a little tantrum!! Like, dayuum!!<br/><br/>Dennis asked me how I was feeling this story. My answer = “it’s nu</span>
  <span id="freeText14206487596331963052" style="display:none">Okay okay okay... Let me ask you this. Do you have kids? Has your child ever freaked out in a restaurant or in a store? If you don’t have kids I bet you’ve thought “lady, get this kid out of here!” And I do! Because 👏🏼 mama 👏🏼 don’t 👏🏼 play 👏🏼! Now, a little tantrum every now and then is normal (believe me, my 5 year old still speaks whinese 🙄) BUT in Baby Teeth by Zoje Stage you get way more than a little tantrum!! Like, dayuum!!<br /><br />Dennis asked me how I was feeling this story. My answer = “it’s nuts, weird, strange but I love it”. For real, this was one wild story and I ate it all up! It made me FEEL so many feels. I was pissed, grossed out, felt creeped out and had me looking at my own child like, huh🤔. <br /><br />So, maybe I should get to the review. Sweet little Hanna is 7 years old and is silent. She loves her daddy, Alex, so much. Mommy, Suzette, is awful and she needs to go. Hanna wants daddy’s attention all to herself. This is told in alternating POV between Hanna and Suzette. <br /><br />Suzette has to homeschool Hanna because she is mute and has been kicked out of multiple schools. She is starting to notice more and more that sweet little Hanna may not be so sweet after all. Her behavior is disturbing in and outside the home. Hanna’s manipulative enough to never let Daddy see her evil schemes. <br /><br />Once Suzette starts mentioning to Alex about their daughter’s behavior he doesn’t believe it. How can his sweet little girl do any of the creepy things that are being described. Even when the schools tell the parents about Hanna’s schemes, Alex isn’t willing to consider it. <br /><br />After reading the final chapter I was smiling. I was like, yassss, Suzette get it! To be honest, if I were Suzette I have no idea what I would do! Your child after you? Creepy AF. I would have set up a camera though and have her set up, but that’s just me and I’m all about that evidence!<br /><br />All in all, I loved it. I like messed up books. Creepy child? Sign me up! Thank you St. Martin’s for sending me a widget of Baby Teeth for an honest review! I recommend! 4.5 stars! Out in July! </span>
  <a data-text-id="14206487596331963052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2318903473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16400687924269367287">4 Disturbingly Good and Twisted Stars to BABY TEETH! <br/><br/>Why I wanted to read this one……This book was a Traveling Sisters Group Read that I missed out on reading and with the so many strong reactions and thoughts towards this book I just knew that I had to read it! I don’t think I have ever been so interested in finding out what my thoughts would be over a book like I was with this one. <br/><br/>So what did I think…….Well, I quite enjoyed it! Now there were a few scenes intended to shock the reader which I t</span>
  <span id="freeText16400687924269367287" style="display:none">4 Disturbingly Good and Twisted Stars to BABY TEETH! <br /><br />Why I wanted to read this one……This book was a Traveling Sisters Group Read that I missed out on reading and with the so many strong reactions and thoughts towards this book I just knew that I had to read it! I don’t think I have ever been so interested in finding out what my thoughts would be over a book like I was with this one. <br /><br />So what did I think…….Well, I quite enjoyed it! Now there were a few scenes intended to shock the reader which I think would definitely make this book not an enjoyable read for some but, for this reader to be totally honest once I read those scenes they were totally forgotten. Until, after finishing the book and then discussing it with Brenda then I was like oh right, I forgot all about those scenes. I was just so entertained in how devious and manipulative Hanna was towards her mother, Suzette that I really needed to know how this story would play out. When I wasn’t reading this book, I was thinking about it.<br /><br />BABY TEETH by ZOJE STAGE is a disturbing, uncomfortable, and downright creepy tale about a 7-year-old girl named Hanna that wants her Daddy all to herself but her Mommy (Suzette) stands in her way of her happily ever after. <br /><br />ZOJE STAGE delivers quite the chilling tale here that was well-written with an easy to read writing style to make this quite the fast-paced read. The story is told in alternating voices and perspectives between Suzette and Hanna, I enjoyed both of their perspectives equally. The things that Hanna was capable of was downright diabolical and creepy! <br /><br />What I didn't like…..The only thing that I questioned here though was if a seven-year-old was actually capable of doing some of the acts that she did in this book.<br /><br />I was totally immersed in this tale and found it quite the entertaining and enjoyable read but I do understand that this book will not be for everyone so with that I recommend with caution. If you love a good horror or a dark psychological thriller you should really enjoy this one though! I know I do and did! <br /><br />Publishing Date: July 17, 2018<br /><br />Thank you so much to NetGalley, Zoje Stage, and St. Martin’s Press for the opportunity to read an advanced copy of this book.<br /><br />Review written and posted on our themed book blog:<br />Two Sisters Lost In A Coulee Reading<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com</a><br /><br />Coulee: a term applied rather loosely to different landforms, all of which refer to a kind of valley.<br />Where I live I am surrounded by Coulees!</span>

  <span id="freeText3534153316558874730" style="display:none">This is one of the creepiest books I've ever read.<br /><br />Hannah is seven years-old and the daughter of Alex and Suzette. She loves her dad but dislikes her mom.<br /><br />Hannah would love to have her dad for herself and starts taking the steps to see this happen. That's the premise of the book and all I can say without getting into spoilers. <br /><br />The book is told from the alternating points of view of Hannah and Suzette. Suzette suffers from Crohn's disease and I found the author described the illness and its symptoms very well, although I don't suffer from it I was able to easily capture the character's constant pain and anguish.<br /><br />Overall, I found the story to be disturbing and had difficulties liking or relating to any of the characters but I still recommend it to readers of psychological thrillers and suspense. <br /><br /><i>I received an advance copy from the publisher via Netgalley </i></span>

<div id="review_2270530782" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2270530782" />
    <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is"><img alt="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516737798p2/4467515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2270530782?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is">Jasmine from How Useful It Is</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=publisher-blog-tour">publisher-blog-tour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2270530782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5548796456226355706"><b>Baby Teeth – Review & Blog Tour</b><br/><br/>About: Baby Teeth is a thriller written by Zoje Stage. It will be published on 7/17/18 by St. Martin’s Press, an imprint of Macmillan Publishers, 320 pages. The genres are thriller, fiction, and mystery. This book is the author’s debut. <br/><br/>My Experience: I started reading Baby Teeth on 2/24/18 and finished it on 3/10/18. This book is an excellent read, though tough topic to handle. I’m reading this book as a mom and I cringe at what Hanna does. I sympathize with Suzet</span>
  <span id="freeText5548796456226355706" style="display:none"><b>Baby Teeth – Review &amp; Blog Tour</b><br /><br />About: Baby Teeth is a thriller written by Zoje Stage. It will be published on 7/17/18 by St. Martin’s Press, an imprint of Macmillan Publishers, 320 pages. The genres are thriller, fiction, and mystery. This book is the author’s debut. <br /><br />My Experience: I started reading Baby Teeth on 2/24/18 and finished it on 3/10/18. This book is an excellent read, though tough topic to handle. I’m reading this book as a mom and I cringe at what Hanna does. I sympathize with Suzette for losing her patience because I would lose it too for Hanna’s intentional bad behaviors. If I were to read this book before having a kid, it would ultimately make a decision for me to never have kids! Though, Hanna’s acting out is understandable for kids that have the demand for fun and games all day long because no one likes to follow rules and do work. This book has both strong views and it’s interesting to unravel as the story move forward.<br /><br />This book is told in the third person point of view following Hanna, 7 years old girl. She hasn’t spoken since the day she was born. Another view is Suzette, Hanna’s mom. Suzette brings Hanna to many doctor appointments to test her for physical and mental problems to figure out why her daughter doesn’t speak. Hanna resents her mom for wanting to send her away to school and leaving her home alone with strangers (babysitters). She punishes her mom by doing opposite of what she’s told to do and more. She terrorizes all babysitters sent her way. Suzette wants her family to be perfect because she didn’t grow up with one. She has a disease called Crohn that gives her bowel movement troubles but her mom didn’t take her in for treatment until too late. This disease caused her to have an unpleasant pregnancy experience. There is a battle between mother and daughter’s relationship that readers can either sympathize or cringe. Suzette tries to be a good mom with patience and rewards for good behaviors, but it’s just impossible not to lose it with Hanna. When Hanna finally speaks, she informs Suzette that she’s not Hanna but Marie-Anne Dufosset, a teen accused of being a witch who was burn to death back in history. Suzette questions her parenting while Hanna makes plans and calculates her next move.<br /><br />A well written thriller, this book can be a mind blowing read. I like the fast paced easy to read writing style. I like the clear picture it paints of a stay-at-home mom with hard work and stress. I like the clear view of a working husband away from the drama at home to be narrow minded and lost in his own beliefs. It’s a frustrating feeling to relate to Suzette when her daughter is only good for her dad and wicked for her. I like following Hanna’s thinking process even though she scares me at times. Suzette’s experience with her disease and parenthood is tough and relatable at times. I would say that this book is disturbing, but I would rather read to know than missing out on it. I would still recommend everyone to read this book, at least once.<br /><br />Pro: fast paced, page turner, easy to read, mom and daughter relationship, parenting, family,<br /><br />Con: none<br /><br />I rate it 5 stars!<br /><br />***Disclaimer: Many thanks to St. Martin’s Press for inviting me to read, review, and host a blog tour for this book. Please be assured that my opinions are honest.<br /><br />xoxo,<br /> Jasmine at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com">www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com</a> for more details<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5548796456226355706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7901341243835151700"><b>3.5 Stars.</b><p>
  <b>Oh dear.....talk about a <b>BAD</b> seed.</b>
</p><p><b>BABY TEETH</b> is quite a horrific story and debut offering....definitely NOT for everyone. I thought I knew where the story was headed...twice....from little hints here and there, but NOPE, the author takes the reader to yet another place....the mind of a disturbed and violent child.</p><p>Seven years old <i>(going on seventeen)</i> Hanna is very astute and conniving, but shows only angelic sweetness to daddy....she REALLY loves her daddy. As a matter-of-fact, she </p></span>
  <span id="freeText7901341243835151700" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars.</b><p>
  <b>Oh dear.....talk about a <b>BAD</b> seed.</b>
</p><p><b>BABY TEETH</b> is quite a horrific story and debut offering....definitely NOT for everyone. I thought I knew where the story was headed...twice....from little hints here and there, but NOPE, the author takes the reader to yet another place....the mind of a disturbed and violent child.</p><p>Seven years old <i>(going on seventeen)</i> Hanna is very astute and conniving, but shows only angelic sweetness to daddy....she REALLY loves her daddy. As a matter-of-fact, she wants to marry him....and in his eyes, well, she's his little <i>silent</i> "squirrelly" girl....most of the time. As for "moody" mommy dearest <i>(who has a truckload of her own issues),</i> Hanna has BIG plans for her....as you will see.</p><p>Told in alternating voices and perspectives of mother Suzette and daughter Hanna, <b>BABY TEETH</b> is a bit long, and there were times I thought lack of parental action a bit bizarre; but hey, this IS a dysfunctional family, and a wild, crazy, creepy journey into the mind of possessiveness and evil.</p><p>Like the classic, The Bad Seed, <i>(that I happen to like)</i> <b>BABY TEETH</b> for me fit right in to that same category of HORROR.</p><p>It is DARK! It is DISTURBING!....so read at your own risk! <i>(Can't wait to read the varied reviews and comments on this one!)</i></p><p>Many thanks to NetGalley and St. Martin's Press for the complimentary ARC COMING JULY, 2018 in exchange for an unbiased review.</p></span>

<div id="review_2277852013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2277852013" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2277852013?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2018-books">2018-books</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2277852013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5319618027076064702">Hanna is seven years old and has yet to speak. She does manage to communicate, though, through malice toward her mother, Suzette. How can Suzette deal with her daughter's psychopathic tendencies when no one believes her?<br/><br/>I got this from Netgalley and the promise of a creepy homicidal kid lured me in. I was a little disappointed.<br/><br/>Like I said in the teaser, Hanna is seven years old, mute, and wishes violence death upon her mother. Suzette is a stay at home mom with Crohn's Disease. Hanna definitely </span>
  <span id="freeText5319618027076064702" style="display:none">Hanna is seven years old and has yet to speak. She does manage to communicate, though, through malice toward her mother, Suzette. How can Suzette deal with her daughter's psychopathic tendencies when no one believes her?<br /><br />I got this from Netgalley and the promise of a creepy homicidal kid lured me in. I was a little disappointed.<br /><br />Like I said in the teaser, Hanna is seven years old, mute, and wishes violence death upon her mother. Suzette is a stay at home mom with Crohn's Disease. Hanna definitely wants mommy out of the way so she can have daddy all to herself. It sounds interesting but I was ultimately bored by most of it.<br /><br />Alex, the dad, is unbelievably oblivious and I thought Suzette was kind of a doormat. How much shit does one person have to eat before they finally do something? Quite a bit, as it turns out. Hanna was interesting but everything she was planning was told from her point of view before it happened so there were very few surprises. I think it would have worked a lot better if we'd never got a glimpse inside Hanna's head. <br /><br />It was engaging enough to finish and Zoje Stage's writing was good in a technical sense. The book made me feel very uneasy at times but that was its biggest accomplishment. I didn't find it suspenseful and by the end I was hoping Hanna would somehow kill both of her parents. Two out of five stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5319618027076064702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Sp06GLwMbmH58GIMf3XPeOXTOUkyU4bmQwS4LqHSf3pJ4bI/OzI98YamTCQlvaIZw3LxphUepRt9/gcxCgLSWA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Zo6tyHEIesG2Qfr7g5/COOnsbbb55Cdv7PTAb4JOiv5l8iXv9jYpUckX1NPZV69Zz02lWd6pBJLSDn9wKZ4n3A==')})
  }

Their closest neighbors are more than two miles in either direction along a rutted dirt road.\n\nOne afternoon, as Wen catches grasshoppers in the front yard, a stranger unexpectedly appears in the driveway. Leonard is the largest man Wen has ever seen but he is young, friendly, and he wins her over almost instantly. Leonard and Wen talk and play until Leonard abruptly apologizes and tells Wen, &quot;None of what’s going to happen is your fault&quot;. Three more strangers then arrive at the cabin carrying unidentifiable, menacing objects. As Wen sprints inside to warn her parents, Leonard calls out: &quot;Your dads won’t want to let us in, Wen. But they have to. We need your help to save the world.&quot;\n\nThus begins an unbearably tense, gripping tale of paranoia, sacrifice, apocalypse, and survival that escalates to a shattering conclusion, one in which the fate of a loving family and quite possibly all of humanity are entwined. The Cabin at the End of the World is a masterpiece of terror and suspense from the fantastically fertile imagination of Paul Tremblay.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"10640878407824174916\" href=\"#\" Bright, ambitious, and yearning for adulthood, fifteen-year-old Vanessa Wye becomes entangled in an affair with Jacob Strane, her magnetic and guileful forty-two-year-old English teacher. \n\n2017. Amid the rising wave of allegations against powerful men, a reckoning is coming due. Strane has been accused of sexual abuse by a former student, who reaches out to Vanessa, and now Vanessa suddenly finds herself facing an impossible choice: remain silent, firm in the belief that her teenage self willingly engaged in this relationship, or redefine herself and the events of her past. But how can Vanessa reject her first love, the man who fundamentally transformed her and has been a persistent presence in her life? Is it possible that the man she loved as a teenager—and who professed to worship only her—may be far different from what she has always believed?\n\nAlternating between Vanessa’s present and her past, My Dark Vanessa juxtaposes memory and trauma with the breathless excitement of a teenage girl discovering the power her own body can wield. Thought-provoking and impossible to put down, this is a masterful portrayal of troubled adolescence and its repercussions that raises vital questions about agency, consent, complicity, and victimhood. Written with the haunting intimacy of The Girls and the creeping intensity of Room, My Dark Vanessa is an era-defining novel that brilliantly captures and reflects the shifting cultural mores   <span id="freeText7776986286951039372" style="display:none">Zoje Stage is the author of WONDERLAND ("mind-bending" - NY Times), and the USA Today and international bestseller, BABY TEETH. Published in the UK under the title BAD APPLE, the novel will soon be available in more than a dozen countries. BABY TEETH was a USA Today bestseller, a People "Book of the Week", and voted by Barnes &amp; Noble, Bloody Disgusting, GoodReads, and Forbes as one of the best horror books of 2018. It was optioned for film by Village Roadshow/Valparaiso Pictures. She lives in Pittsburgh, PA.</span>
